+------------------------+

1) Welcome to the new and somewhat different bestiary for Final Fantasy IV,
part of the new Final Fantasy IV Complete Collection. I was thrilled to hear
that FF4 was going to get the treatment which FF1 and 2 got on the PSP a few
years back. What made it even better was the sequel was to be added into it
all. And to top it all off despite coming out in Japan a few weeks before the
US release it was already fully in English. Took a long time to find a way to
get a copy instead of waiting and finally did, and been spending many a day
with it. And now I decided to do the bestiary for FF4 which I played through
first.

Although the game has been out for almost 9 months now, and most people already
know this I suppose I'll say it anyway. Your bestiary file is not tied into the
save game like FF4 Advance was. It is saved as a seperate file called System
Data. That file stores the bestiary data for all 3 games as well. Another thing
to mention is to make sure you keep regular multiple saves if you're shooting
to complete the bestiary in one playthrough. You get 20 saves in FF4 and 40 in
TAY to use. As mentioned before with the system data file, your bestiary will
always be up to date, should you be playing a save file 5 hours behind your
main save, or 10 hours later after getting a missing entry from another save
game.

If you have any questions or comments about this, or for FF4 in general, feel
free to email me.

Cal_96@hotmail.com

You are free to use this file for help on the game, and please feel free to
post it on a web site, as long as the file remains in tact and is unaltered.
I would hate to see my hard work go to a waste by someone trying to reword it
and change the format and call it their own. If you do use this on a web site,
please send me an email letting me know that you want to use it.

2) Notes

4-19-11

Finished the Bestiary. Took longer than anticipated, although a lot of the
work was just copy/paste from other things. Most of this is done and can be
used. I just need to add the locations where you can find the monsters, and
perhaps play through the GBA content again to finish up the notes on some of
the bosses there. This is mostly done from memory and will probably need to
be looked at again. The Bestiary was done using the Japan version of the game,
but will compare it with the US version as soon as the stores here actually
get it in so I can buy it. Will further update using the US version if needed.

Finished the Interlude and TAY additions to the Bestiary. Whole thing is

4-30-11

In the previous update notes, I said something about the file getting a bit
messy. Well I tried to make it a formatted FAQ, and it didn't quite turn out
so well. First of all I mean it did look nice, and would probably look great
when finished. But it would be very time consuming to go through and edit and
double check 13548 lines (although it will be more after this update) to make
sure I didn't forget anything. Second I don't think you can download a file
formatted in this way. True enough you can print it out, but I don't know how
may people would go that way. Seems like a waste of paper to me. I also like
for the readers of my FAQs and what not to have the option of downloading them
should they wish. That is why I chose to keep this Bestiary as it. :)

get some done on it now and then, but its still really hard to do.

Now as I try to play FF4 again, I find myself having to change a few things.
For some reason, in the Japanese version of the game, #42 is a Ghoul. In the US
version its a Wraith. Type Insect in the Japanese version is Beast in US
version. Good thing I noticed that one. Aside from the name differences, the
stats are identical. I'll have to keep my eyes open for that in Interlude and
TAY as I play through them again.

4) Basic Info

The bestiary will be comprised in a chart format. I have decided to do it as
the monsters appear, rather than alphabetical. That way if you are looking for
say entry #130, you can find it easier, rather than looking for either #129 or
#131 and find them way at the top or bottom of the list cause their names start
with A or Z.

The charts will basically look something like this:

 _____________________________
|                             |
|Number:                      |
|Name:                        |
|Slain:                       |
|HP:                          |
|Strength:                    |
|Defense:                     |
|Magic:                       |
|Magic Def.:                  |
|Gil:                         |
|EXP:                         |
|Treasure:                    |
|T1                           |
|T2                           |
|T3                           |
|T4                           |
|Type:                        |
 _____________________________
|                             |
|Weakness:                    |
|Resistance*:                 |
|Leech**:                     |
 _____________________________

Notes:
Location:

*: Pretty sure resistance is the same as immunity.
**: For some reason absorbing damage as HP is listed in this game as Leech
rather than absorb. Just noting that as not to confuse anyone.

Now a quick breakdown as to what all this means.

Number: The number of the monster, as listed by the bestiary.
Name: The name of the monster.
Slain: The number of monsters you have killed. (Won't be listed)
HP: The amount of HP the monster has.
Strength: The amount of attack power the monster has.
Defense: The amount of defense power or armor a monster has.
Magic: The amount of power a monster has behind its magic. Or perhaps how much
MP a monster has? Of course they never run out so I dunno on this one for sure.
Magic Def: The amount of defense against magic a monster has.
Gil: The amount of Gil you get for killing the monster.
EXP: The amount of Exp you get for killing the monster.
This is the base value, so take EXP divided by number of surviving party
members for actual value.
Treasure: The items the monster may drop after killing it. T1 is far more
likely to drop than say T4. In the chart, it will not say T1 it will just say
Potion.
Type: The category in which the monster belongs. Some weapons will inflict
more damage to certain types. Some armor reduces damage by certain types.

Weakness: The type of magic or weapon a monster is weak to.
Resistance: The type of status affects a monster is immune to.
Leech: The element that will heal the monster. Weapon attacks do not heal it
however.

Notes: A few tidbits of information about the monster if anything important.
Location: The location where you can find the monsters at.

***Important Info about Lunar Ruins***

The Lunar Ruins are probably one of the most annoying dungeons ever. It seems
every floor is randomized and probably never the same twice through. Therefore
I am not sure how accurate my information on finding the monsters down there
will be. Just because I ran into X on a moonlike floor at the start will mean
that you will too. I'll try my best on it but can't make any promises. The only
thing that makes sense is when you go down, you'll come to the character rooms
in this order (The floor number is in the () in case you wonder what that is):
              Start
               Yang(4)
             Edward(8)
             Rydia(12)
             Cecil(16)
              Rosa(20)
              Edge(24)
              Kain(28)
               Cid(32)
            Twins*(36)

*Requires both in party at same time

Some monsters may appear further down, so that may assist you in finding them.
There are also some monsters specific to each character room.

5a) Bestiary - Interlude

2/21/12

This is the full and completed Bestiary for Interlude. All monster locations
have now been added. There are a couple missable monsters, and a couple that
take a lot of patience and even more luck to find. That being said, I advise
you to make use of all 5 save files in various parts of the game, in case you
missed one and want to get 100% without starting over.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Here is the info for the chart again, if you just skipped down to this part.

 _____________________________
|                             |
|Number:                      |
|Name:                        |
|Slain:                       |
|HP:                          |
|Strength:                    |
|Defense:                     |
|Magic:                       |
|Magic Def.:                  |
|Gil:                         |
|EXP:                         |
|Treasure:                    |
|T1                           |
|T2                           |
|T3                           |
|T4                           |
|Type:                        |
 _____________________________
|                             |
|Weakness:                    |
|Resistance*:                 |
|Leech**:                     |
 _____________________________

Notes:

*: Pretty sure resistance is the same as immunity.
**: For some reason absorbing damage as HP is listed in this game as Leech
rather than absorb. Just noting that as not to confuse anyone.

Now a quick breakdown as to what all this means.

Number: The number of the monster, as listed by the bestiary.
Name: The name of the monster.
Slain: The number of monsters you have killed. (Won't be listed)
HP: The amount of HP the monster has.
Strength: The amount of attack power the monster has.
Defense: The amount of defense power or armor a monster has.
Magic: The amount of power a monster has behind its magic. Or perhaps how much
MP a monster has? Of course they never run out so I dunno on this one for sure.
Magic Def: The amount of defense against magic a monster has.
Gil: The amount of Gil you get for killing the monster.
EXP: The amount of Exp you get for killing the monster.
This is the base value, so take EXP divided by number of surviving party
members for actual value.
Treasure: The items the monster may drop after killing it. T1 is far more
likely to drop than say T4. In the chart, it will not say T1 it will just say
Potion.
Type: The category in which the monster belongs. Some weapons will inflict
more damage to certain types. Some armor reduces damage by certain types.

Weakness: The type of magic or weapon a monster is weak to.
Resistance: The type of status affects a monster is immune to.
Leech: The element that will heal the monster. Weapon attacks do not heal it
however.

Notes: A few tidbits of information about the monster if anything important.
Location: The location where you can find the monsters at.

*NOTES*

Once you start the Tower of Babil on floor B1 with Edge, the following entries
in the Bestiary can be found. However, if you advance the game by entering the
tower before getting them, you'll have to either start over or use an earlier
save as there is no going back from this point.

Missable entries: 24, 27, 28, 29
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
5b) Bestiary - TAY

Here is the Bestiary for The After Years. As of this date (3/21/12) I should now
have all the entries from Ceodore's and Rydia's story and CD completed. From the
previous version of the Bestiary, all monster names and stats are completed,
just not the locations yet.

Notes: Monsters all seem to have less strength and some less magic than in
the original game. Perhaps this is due to the effects of the moon phase.
Not much difference in EXP but there is some changes in Gil, mostly less in
value. Certain treasures have changed as well.

As with FF4 and Interlude, I suggest you make use of the 40 save slots. That
way if you mess up and miss an entry, you can always go back and get it at a
later time. I've seen this a lot at the Gamefaqs.com message boards, and if you
are playing the first time, make a NEW save file each time you finish a story.
At the end of the game, you should have at least 9 save files from all the
stories with a star (*) next to it. While not really needed, it does make the
final story more enjoyable.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Here is a brief cheat sheet that I will be updating as soon as I start playing
TAY again. It will list each character's story, and the number of each entry
you can find in it. If its marked with a *, then it is post story content, such
as the Challenge Dungeons (CD from now on). I will be playing the stories in the
order they are listed from the game menu. Even if enemies appear in multiple
stories, the first time it shows up as NEW! will be the story I list its
location in. The number inside () just shows what % of the bestiary should be
at if you've located all the monsters (hopefully I won't have to go back and
mess with that part too much).

         41, 44, 45, 46, 47*, 48, 49, 50, 52, 53, 54, 55, 56, 57*, 58, 59, 61,
         63, 64, 66, 68, 71*, 72*, 77*, 79, 80, 81*, 82, 83*, 87, 90*, 94*,
         100*, 103*, 107*, 110*, 131*, 136, 141*, 157, 158, 159, 160, 161, 162,

For a more detailed look at where to find all the entries, look at the bestiary
below.

Again if you just did a Ctrl +F to get here, this is how the monster charts
will look, and a brief explaination of the terms within it.

 _____________________________
|                             |
|Number:                      |
|Name:                        |
|Slain:                       |
|HP:                          |
|Strength:                    |
|Defense:                     |
|Magic:                       |
|Magic Def.:                  |
|Gil:                         |
|EXP:                         |
|Treasure:                    |
|T1                           |
|T2                           |
|T3                           |
|T4                           |
|Type:                        |
 _____________________________
|                             |
|Weakness:                    |
|Resistance*:                 |
|Leech**:                     |
 _____________________________

Notes:

*: Pretty sure resistance is the same as immunity.
**: For some reason absorbing damage as HP is listed in this game as Leech
rather than absorb. Just noting that as not to confuse anyone.

Now a quick breakdown as to what all this means.

Number: The number of the monster, as listed by the bestiary.
Name: The name of the monster.
Slain: The number of monsters you have killed. (Won't be listed)
HP: The amount of HP the monster has.
Strength: The amount of attack power the monster has.
Defense: The amount of defense power or armor a monster has.
Magic: The amount of power a monster has behind its magic. Or perhaps how much
MP a monster has? Of course they never run out so I dunno on this one for sure.
Magic Def: The amount of defense against magic a monster has.
Gil: The amount of Gil you get for killing the monster.
EXP: The amount of Exp you get for killing the monster.
This is the base value, so take EXP divided by number of surviving party
members for actual value.
Treasure: The items the monster may drop after killing it. T1 is far more
likely to drop than say T4. In the chart, it will not say T1 it will just say
Potion.
Type: The category in which the monster belongs. Some weapons will inflict
more damage to certain types. Some armor reduces damage by certain types.

Weakness: The type of magic or weapon a monster is weak to.
Resistance: The type of status affects a monster is immune to.
Leech: The element that will heal the monster. Weapon attacks do not heal it
however.

Notes: A few tidbits of information about the monster if anything important.
Location: The location where you can find the monsters at. Since TAY is story
based unlike the previous games, this section will look like this:

Location: (Character) Location name {Moon Phase} &lt;M:N/Y/P&gt;
Character: Which character's story the monster is found in.
Location name: The name of the map it is found in. (Be sure to check your menu
for the names if needed.)
Moon Phase: Only applies to some monsters. This IS the moon phase you need to
be in to find said monster. If there is no moon phase, it can be found in all
phases. Will either be New, Full, Waxing or Waning.
M: Its getting long but this is short for missable. Its either N (no), Y (yes),
or P (possible). No means the monster can be found over the course of the game,
although some may take a while to find. Yes means they can be missed, either
killing some monsters too fast or too slow. Possible means they can be missed
simply by looking in the wrong moon phase or missing a treasure chest. As there
are NPCs in towns that tell you some of this info, this applies mostly to the
last chapters where no such info can be found.

Notes: A bit of a tough entry here. You need to beat him without having both
Asura and Leviathan from earlier in game. If you have them both, you can't
get him into the bestiary. And given the fact that its 15-20 floors between
those two places and many bosses as well it requires a lot of time if you want
to go for 100% in the bestiary.

But back to the bestiary. Standard Bahamaut. Will cast Megaflare after a 5
second countdown.

Notes: Accompanied by a Steel Golem and Mythril Golem. Uses a pretty strong
Beam attack when golems are alive. When golems are defeated it will use
Meltdown which is a Self-Destruct attack on the whole party. Given it has 10000
HP and this attack's damage is based on remaining HP, it can almost certainly
wipe out the party. use caution when dealing with this one as I have found out.

<script type="text/javascript">

window.onhashchange = hashHasChanged;

function hashHasChanged()
{
	$(document).scrollTop(window.pageYOffset-130);
}

$().ready(function()
{
	$('.faq_bookmark_jumper').clone().appendTo('#faq_header_wrap');
	if(window.pageYOffset>=150)
	{
		$('#faq_header_wrap').addClass('fixed');
	}

	window.onscroll = function()
	{
		if(window.pageYOffset>=150)
		{
			$('#faq_header_wrap').addClass('fixed');
			$('.top_link').addClass('fixed').css('display','block');
		}
		else
		{
			$('#faq_header_wrap').removeClass('fixed');
			$('.top_link').removeClass('fixed').css('display','none');
		}
	};

	
	$.each($('.ffaq img.imgnofloat'),function(){
		var image = $(this);
		if(image.attr('width')>400)
		{
			image.addClass('bigresize');
		}
	});

	
	var autobm = window.setInterval(function()
	{
		if(window.pos==$(document).scrollTop() || window.autobmstop==true)
			clearInterval(autobm);
		else
			set_bookmark(1);
	}, 5000);
});


$('img.imgresize').bind('click touch', function()
{
	if($(this).css('max-width')=='none')
		$(this).css({'width':'100%','max-width':'100%'});
	else
		$(this).css({'width':'auto','max-width':'none'});
});

var timer, lastsearch;

$('body :not(#faq_search_results)').bind('click touch', function(e)
{
	if($('#faq_search_results').css('display')=='block')
	{
		e.stopPropagation();
		if($(this).attr('id')!='results_table' && $(this).attr('id')!='faq_search' && $(this).attr('id')!='faq_search_input' && $(this).attr('class')!='head' && $(this).attr('id')!='home_links')
		{
			dismiss_faq_search_results(0);
		}
	}
});

$('#faq_search_input, .search_mobile').click(function(e)
{
	e.preventDefault();
	if($(this).attr('class')=='search_mobile')
	{
		$('#faq_search_module').toggle();
	}
	$('#faq_search_module, #faq_search_results').addClass('fixed');
	$('#faq_header_wrap').addClass('search');
	
	if($('#faq_search_results').css('display')!='block')
	{
		$('#faq_search_results').show();
	}
	if($('#results_table tr').length==0)
		$('.close_results').hide();
	$('#faq_search_input').focus();
});

$('#faq_search_input').keyup(function()
{
	if(lastsearch != $('#faq_search_input').val())
	{
		if(timer)
			clearTimeout(timer);
		lastsearch = $('#faq_search_input').val();
		if($('#faq_search_input').val().length>=3)
		{
			$('#faq_search_results').show();
			timer = setTimeout(function(){faq_search(62210, $('#faq_search_input').val())},150);
		}
		else
		{
			dismiss_faq_search_results(1);
		}
	}
});

function dismiss_faq_search_results(fixed)
{
	$('#faq_search_results').hide();
	$('#faq_search_overlay').fadeTo(200,0).remove();
	if(!fixed)
	{
		$('#faq_search_module, #faq_search_results').removeClass('fixed');
		$('#faq_header_wrap').removeClass('search');
		if($('.search_mobile').is(':visible'))
			$('#faq_search_module').toggle();
	}
	$('#results_table').empty();
}

function search_result(row)
{
	if($('#results_table tr[data-row="'+row+'"]').length>0)
	{
		var url = $('#results_table tr[data-row="'+row+'"]').attr('data-url');
		if(url.indexOf('search_highlight')>=0)
			eval(url);
		else
			window.location = $('#results_table tr[data-row="'+row+'"]').attr('data-url');
	}
}

$('body :not(#faq_toc_header *, #faq_toc a.toc_toggle *)').bind('click touch', function(e)
{
	if($('#faq_toc_header').css('display')=='block')
	{
		e.stopPropagation();
		if($(this).attr('class')!='toc_toggle active' && $(this).attr('id')!='faq_toc_header')
		{
			$('.toc_toggle').removeClass('active');
			$('#faq_toc_header').css('display','none');
		}
	}
});

function toc_toggle()
{
	if($('.toc_toggle').hasClass('active'))
	{
		$('a.toc_toggle').removeClass('active');
		$('#faq_toc_header').css('display','none');
	}
	else
	{
		$('a.toc_toggle').addClass('active');
		$('#faq_toc_header').css('display','block');
	}
}

function faq_search(id, term)
{
	var term = $('#faq_search_input').val();
	var len = term.length;
	if(term.length<3)
		return;

	$.ajax(
	{
		type: 'POST',
		url: '/ajax/faq_search',
		data:  {id: 62210, term: term, key: '66dfc62a'},
		success: function(response)
		{
			if(response[0]=='error')
			{
				$('#results_table').html('<tr><td colspan="2" class="dismiss_results"><span onclick="dismiss_faq_search_results(0);">No Results Found - Close</span></td></tr>');
				$('.close_results').remove();
				$('#faq_search_results').show();
			}
			else
			{
				window.currentpage = 0;
				$('#results_table').html('');
				$('.close_results').remove();

				$.each(response,function(j,i)
				{
					var val = i.value;
					val = val.split('-');
					var page = val[0];
					
					if(window.currentpage!=page)
					{
						window.currentpage = page;
					}
					var link, pagenum = '';

					
					
					{
						link = "search_highlight(62210,"+val[0]+",2,"+val[1]+","+len+");";
					}
					

					$('#results_table').append('<tr data-url="'+link+'" data-row="'+j+'" style="cursor:pointer;" onclick="search_result('+j+');"><td class="title">'+i.label+'</td><td class="type">'+pagenum+'</td></tr>');
				});

				$('#results_table').after('<div onclick="dismiss_faq_search_results(0);" class="close_results">Close Results</div>');
			}
		}
	});
}

function search_highlight(file_id,page,format,pos,len,section)
{
	window.textpage = page+1;

	$.ajax(
	{
		type: 'POST',
		url: '/ajax/faq_search_highlight',
		data: { id: file_id, page: page, for: format, pos: pos, len: len, section: '', key: '66dfc62a' },
		success: function(response)
		{
					$('span[name="search_jump"]').remove();
			$("span.faq_highlight").contents().unwrap();
			$('pre#faqspan-'+window.textpage).html(response);
		
		$.each($('.ffaq img.imgnofloat'),function(){
			var image = $(this);
			if(image.attr('width')>400)
			{
				image.addClass('bigresize');
			}
		});
		var offset = $('span[name="search_jump"]').offset().top - 100;
		if(offset<100)
			$(document).scrollTop(0);
		else
			$(document).scrollTop(offset);
		}
	});
}



function set_bookmark(auto)
{
	var pos = $(document).scrollTop();
	if(pos!=window.pos)
		window.pos = pos;
	else
		return;
	var page = 0;
	if(page!=window.page)
		window.page = page;
	if(auto)
		auto = 1;
	$.ajax(
	{
		type: 'POST',
		url: '/ajax/faq_bookmark',
		data: { id: 62210, pid: 615911, pos: pos, page: page, section: '', auto: auto, key: '66dfc62a' },
		success: function(response)
		{
			if(response)
			{
				if(response=="Missing cookie.")
					window.autobmstop = true;
				$('.faq_bookmark_jump').fadeOut();
				$('#faq_bookmark').addClass('active');
				var html = $('.bm_jumper_inner').html();
				$('.bm_jumper_inner').animate({'opacity':0},200,function()
				{
					if($('.faq_bookmark_jumper:not(.active)'))
						$('.faq_bookmark_jumper').css('visibility','visible');
					$(this).html('Bookmark Saved').animate({'opacity':1},200);
					$('.faq_bookmark_jumper').animate({'opacity':1},200);
				});
				setTimeout(function()
				{
					if($('.faq_bookmark_jumper:not(.active)'))
					{
						$('.faq_bookmark_jumper').animate({'opacity':0},200,function()
						{
							$(this).css('visibility','hidden');
						});
					}
					$('.bm_jumper_inner').animate({'opacity':0},200,function()
					{
						$(this).html($.trim(html)).animate({'opacity':1},200);
					});
				}, 3000);
			}
		}
	});
}

function bookmark_jump_dismiss()
{
	$('#faq_header > .faq_bookmark_jumper').css('visibility','hidden');
	$('#faq_header_wrap > .faq_bookmark_jumper').remove();
	$('#faq_bookmark').removeClass('active');
}



function page_top()
{
	$(window).scrollTop(0);
}

function make_printable()
{
	var faqdiv = $('#faqtext').detach();
	faqdiv.appendTo('#fullscreen_overlay');
	$('#fullscreen_overlay').show();
	$('.wrapper').hide();
	$('#faqtext').addClass("fullscreen_takeover");
	$('#faqtext').append('<p id="restore_page"><button onclick="restore_page();">Restore Page</button></p>');
	$(window).scrollTop(0);
}

function restore_page()
{
	$('#restore_page').remove();
	$('#faqtext').removeClass("fullscreen_takeover");
	$('#fullscreen_overlay').hide();
	$('.wrapper').show();
	var faqdiv = $('#faqtext').detach();
	faqdiv.appendTo('#faqwrap');
	$(window).scrollTop(0);
}



function set_rec_val(val)
{
	
	var ftype = "guide";	
	$('#recval').val(val);
	if(val==2)
		$('.rec_comment').attr('placeholder','What is missing from this '+ftype+'? (140 character max)');
	$('#rec_one').hide();
	$('#rec_two').show();
	return;
}

function hide_rec()
{
	$('#rec_two').hide();
	$('#rec_three').show();
	var timer = setTimeout(function()
	{
		$('#contrib_rec').fadeOut('slow').remove();
		$('#faq_header_wrap').addClass('rec_closed');
	}, 2000);
}

function rec_submit(item_id, item_type_id, button)
{
	var recval = $('#recval').val();
	if($('.rec_comment'))
		var reccommentval = $('.rec_comment').val();
	else
		var reccommentval = '';

	$.ajax(
	{
		type: 'POST',
		url: '/ajax/gamespace_contrib_rec',
		data: { item: item_id, type: item_type_id, btn: button, val: recval, comment: reccommentval, key: '66dfc62a' },
		success: function(response)
		{
			if(response==2)
			{
				track_event(79);
				return;
			}
			else
				hide_rec();
		}
	});
}

</script>
